Jiangsu Province War Zone Relief Association Begs for Medicine 101

The Jiangsu Province War Zone Relief Committee sent a letter to various agencies, stating: "Regarding this matter, since the Jiading, Taicang, and Baoshan war zones have experienced the devastation of war, the people have been displaced and migrated, and those who have luckily escaped death are groaning in bed. Since the beginning of summer, the weather has been extremely hot and epidemics have occurred. After a major war, there will inevitably be a major epidemic, and the spread of infection is especially expected. Our association has sent a letter to the National Government's Shanghai War Zone Post-Disaster Preparatory Committee, requesting that the Epidemic Prevention Group find ways to prevent epidemics and establish epidemic prevention hospitals in Jiading, Nanxiang, Huangdu, Baoshan, Kunshan, and other places, and separately dispatch personnel to administer vaccinations. However, the area is vast and the population is large, and it is difficult to provide universal vaccination. Those who die of epidemics in remote areas are still unable to receive assistance. We have always admired your enthusiasm for public welfare and your miraculous effectiveness in preparing medicines for Sha and epidemic diseases. Shi Liangcai, Zhang Jiaao, and Zhu Qinglan, Standing Committee Members of the Jiangsu Province War Zone Relief Committee.

The Telephone at the Customs Zhanghuabang Watchtower Has Been Repaired Yesterday 102

The Wusong Zhanghuabang Watchtower, which is under the jurisdiction of the Customs River Affairs Department, is used to manage the entry and exit of ships and report the hanging of signs at the Bund Customs Pier via telephone, in order to facilitate passengers. Since the Japanese army invaded Zhabei on the evening of January 28th, the telephone line was cut off the next day, making direct calls impossible. Also, due to being within the line of fire, it was inconvenient to repair. Therefore, the Yangshupu Lan Road Watchtower was used for observation instead. It has been more than half a year. Yesterday, it was heard that the telephone at the Zhanghuabang Watchtower was repaired at 5:00 PM. From now on, the entry and exit of ships will still be reported by Zhanghuabang.

Page 15

Local News II

Li Guojie Organizes Specific Plans for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company 104

Pained Account of Past Corruption

Detailed Explanation of the Fundamental Reorganization Plan

Submitted to the Supervisor for Approval and Implementation

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is the leading shipping enterprise in our country, but it is like a body suffering from a long illness, riddled with holes, on the verge of death, with debts accumulated to over seventeen million taels. Its business has declined to its lowest point, with excessive staff, many dilapidated ships and warehouses, and countless instances of corruption. Since Mr. Li Guojie took office as general manager, he has strived for fundamental reorganization to save shipping rights. He has submitted a report to Chen Fumu, Vice Minister of Transportation and Supervisor of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, detailing the current real situation, how to reorganize, and the reorganization plan and implementation steps, offering his opinions for consideration and requesting instructions. The original text is recorded below:

The Current Real Situation. The following is respectfully submitted to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to report on the real situation, the general overview of the inspection and reorganization since taking office, and a proposed fundamental reorganization plan, requesting review, approval, and implementation. Today's China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is like a body suffering from a long illness, riddled with holes, on the verge of death. Outsiders are unaware of the truth and still believe that it has hidden wealth and regard it as a lucrative post, vying to share in it. Once they enter the company and witness all the abuses, they think of reform but have no time. They personally experience all kinds of difficulties and want to eliminate them but have no power, so they suffer as if bearing a great burden and sitting on pins and needles. Since 1928, although I, Guojie, have remained in the position of chairman of the board, I have had no say in the company's personnel and administration. Everything was isolated. At that time, there was much talk about reorganization, but I never expected that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's condition would become so severe. Since taking office, I have carefully inspected and realized that this disease has penetrated deep into the bone marrow and reached the final and most serious stage, which is far beyond my usual expectations. In terms of debt, it has accumulated to more than seventeen million taels, an increase of more than one-third compared to before. The number is truly alarming. As for interest, some is long overdue and has not been paid, and some has been repeatedly postponed for both principal and interest but has always been in arrears, resulting in creditors constantly demanding payment and leaving no peace. In particular, the HSBC Bank is the largest creditor. Recently, due to the large amount of overdue interest, it has demanded the return of the entire principal and interest of the loan, about seven million taels, according to the original contract. Last year, because it was promised to be repaid by the end of the year, the pressure to repay has become more urgent than before because of the inability to pay. They have the right to dispose of the collateral, and we are in danger of bankruptcy. After repeated negotiations by the board of directors, it is fortunate that there has been no breakdown yet, but how can we continue to evade this with empty words? This is the biggest problem. In terms of business, the main source of income is the cargo carried. However, due to poor communication with merchants, ships often fail to be fully loaded. Furthermore, there are cases of underreporting, understating weight, classifying goods incorrectly and using inaccurate sizes. Bills of lading and customs declarations are often inconsistent. This kind of corruption has been accumulating for a long time, and the leakage is almost half. The branch offices in various ports still use the old system of package payments for cargo freight, or they have switched to reporting actual expenses. There is no unified method. As a result, the cunning embezzle at will, and the weak use the excuse of compensation, deceiving each other, which is very unreasonable. Although there are quotas for cargo brokers to pay for passenger tickets, because the guarantee deposit is too large, they regard it as unchangeable. If there is a surplus, they consider it their private income, and if there is a deficit, they claim that they cannot afford to compensate. Furthermore, because they are greedy for a full load, they overcharge for tickets, and gradually exceed their authority, starting the anchor and berthing at ports. The captain's authority has gradually been taken over by the cargo brokers. As for the collection of small freight fees, the original intention was to prevent the smuggling of brokers, but smuggling has not been prevented and is difficult to prevent. Furthermore, they openly smuggle private goods and seize cabin space, so that each voyage of the ships on the river and sea loses money. Even if they do not lose money, there is not much profit to speak of. In addition, the country is in turmoil, and there are frequent requisitions, with wounded soldiers and scattered soldiers being sent here and there, almost using the ships as homes. Therefore, monthly expenses are high during requisitions, and even the income from ordinary business is often not enough to cover expenses, with a shortfall of tens of thousands. This is the second biggest problem. In terms of personnel, since the division of departments and sections, the number of personnel has been increasing day by day, and expenses have also been expanding. Take the tea servers on each ship as an example, each time a cargo broker is changed, a new group is added. The old ones cannot be removed due to the interference of the labor union. If the handling is too strict, there will be a storm. As a result, the number of staff increases day by day, causing abuses. The heads of various branch offices use the excessive advance payments as a protective talisman. Although they know that they are not very competent, it is not easy to replace them. As for the position of the navigator, it is related to the lives and property of the entire ship. How important it is! The New China ship was wrecked the year before last because of the use of a second mate with no technical experience, causing great damage. However, various parties do not understand and regard the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company as an ordinary agency, thinking that it is irrelevant to academics, and they can easily place idle personnel here. As a result, they ask for vacancies, and the gifts pile up. If they are not satisfied, it often causes misunderstandings and severe criticism. This is the third biggest problem. In terms of ships and warehouses, most of them are dilapidated and urgently need repair. An inspection of the existing company ships shows that there are only twenty-five ships, and less than half of them are in good condition and suitable for use. The rest are too old, run slowly, have insufficient tonnage for loading, and consume twice as much coal. In recent years, although they have been repaired from time to time, the materials and labor are all substandard, and the repair costs are wasted. The warehouses and ships are still in the old style and are mostly dilapidated, with limited storage capacity. The authorities groan and become haggard in the midst of economic difficulties. All fundamental plans such as adding ships, building warehouses, and upgrading wharves are beyond their ability. They simply let the new ones gradually become old and the old ones gradually become abandoned. What is even more regrettable is that the central government is thinking about reorganizing the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, but the bad habits of theft and leakage on various ships and warehouses have not been eliminated at all. Not only does the public suffer abuses, but merchants also suffer frequent losses. This is the fourth biggest problem. In terms of assets, whether they are complete shipping assets or various real estate unrelated to the shipping industry, they have not been fundamentally reorganized and are allowed to be abandoned, no different from barren fields. It is a pity. For example, various wharves and docks should have been upgraded and cultivated long ago to exploit the land. However, following the old ways, year after year, what initially would have cost only 50,000 taels to upgrade and build, later increased to 300,000 taels. Now, it is no longer possible to do it for 600,000 or 700,000 taels. Land prices are soaring and changing rapidly. In this intangible way, I don't know how much profit has been abandoned. The wharves and warehouses operated by various foreign companies in our country are not worth mentioning. Just look at the Gonghexiang Wharf near the North Station. Since the upgrade, the tall buildings have stood high and the momentum is magnificent. Compared to it, we should feel ashamed. Also, the houses along Fuzhou Road are small and narrow and urgently need to be rebuilt. Ten-story buildings can be built, with one or two floors for the company's office use, and the rest can be leased at a high price. On the Bund, one can see the tall buildings of various large commercial firms, standing tall and majestic. Compared to these short houses that have not progressed for a long time, it is like wearing worn-out clothes standing next to someone wearing fox fur, which is very shameful. In today's land where every inch is worth gold, there is no plan to develop and generate profits. Only debts are troublesome, and expenses are short. After much thought, I plan to sell some of the assets to obtain a large amount of cash to alleviate the temporary difficulties. Therefore, there is a theory of selling assets to save shipping. I don't know that the company's assets that can be sold are all wharves and land protecting the wharves, which are related to the fate of the shipping industry. It is impossible to sell them. As for assets unrelated to the shipping industry, there are not many of them. At most, the value is only a few million. Furthermore, under the current circumstances of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, it is difficult to find a buyer. Moreover, the property deeds have all been pledged to creditors and are subject to restrictions. Even if some property prices are obtained, they must be deducted to repay the debt first. We will still have little left in our hands, only to regret it. Therefore, instead of eagerly seeking ways to generate profits from assets, we only diligently seek to divide the profits of the organization, eating away at the foundation, which is a great taboo in business. This is the fifth biggest problem.

Implementation of Reorganization. The above five problems have either already erupted externally or are still lurking internally, and are enough to lead to the death of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. I, Guojie, see this dangerous situation and feel that I have no way to deal with it. Furthermore, when I was hastily appointed, it happened to be after the outbreak of the Shanghai war, and the financial situation was even more exhausted. The salaries of employees and sailors have been in arrears for almost two months. The company's daily water and electricity and other necessary needs are almost exhausted. Only one coal company is still willing to do business with us. Hardware must be purchased in cash in small quantities. The total amount of repair fees and goods and labor payments owed to various factories is tens of thousands. The cash handed over by the previous general manager was only two thousand or so, while the bad checks were over 400,000, some of which were due and some of which were due soon. I was unwilling to wear a broken hat. In addition, the nature of this company is uncertain, causing many doubts and concerns. Standing on this position, it is even more difficult to cope with, and handling affairs is even more difficult. Only by upholding the spirit of reorganization of the Ministry of Transportation and the supervision, and bearing the earnest entrustment of the shareholders, and remembering the hard work of the ancestors in creating this company, I, Guojie, bear a heavy responsibility for this company, and my fate is closely related to it. Now that I am focusing on reorganization, how dare I be afraid of difficulties and seek complacency? I have to try my best to seek treatment, hoping to achieve a little effect. However, the disease is deep and the accumulation is difficult to reverse. To deal with it perfunctorily will not help, and to apply strong medicine rashly will also lead to disaster. The only plan is to make a fundamental and conscientious plan and gradually seek salvation. The current palliative measures must be carried out step by step in order to be effective. However, it will take time and a longer period. It cannot be fully expressed. It is impossible to cure a dying body with one medicine. It is impossible to run fast with a cane. Now the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has too much debt and too many disputes. Each problem takes weeks or months to find a solution. If the political tide is transferred and the authorities advance and retreat together, the plan will be determined and the foundation will be shaken. I can only respectfully refuse to pay. I will briefly present to you the reorganization process that has been planned and organized in the past three months, starting with palliative treatment. (1) Debt. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's heavy debt and bad credit have been mentioned above. The government has no large amount of money to subsidize, and the shareholders lack the financial resources to increase capital. We have reached the end of our rope. In the business world, only those with strong capital can control everything. Otherwise, they can only rely on personal strength and reputation to deal with all parties. The reason why various creditors are becoming increasingly tight is that they do not trust me, and I have no practical way to inform them. Now, I am contacting various domestic and foreign creditor groups separately, starting with connecting feelings, clearing up misunderstandings, being open and honest, distinguishing between urgency, and negotiating phased repayments. I will also convert various dead debts into living debts. For those assets that were not fully mortgaged before, I will raise some loans to provide turnover, hoping to restore credit. The creditors know that I have a practical solution and show some understanding. Now, the two months' salaries owed to employees and sailors by the previous general manager have been raised and paid, and the overdue checks have also been paid separately. In the midst of the stagnant atmosphere, it is fortunate that a slight sign of life has appeared. (2) Business. I am now supervising the responsible personnel to focus on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and the Min and Guangdong areas to develop business. On the one hand, I am conscientiously connecting business information and soliciting cargo. On the other hand, I am strictly auditing and preventing embezzlement. Various branch offices and ships and warehouses are gradually being improved. I have also formulated sound and practical measures, and re-measured the cabin space of each ship and set up charts so that the cabin volume and cargo weight can be calculated according to the charts at a glance. Furthermore, the two matters of review and investigation are extremely beneficial to increasing profits and eliminating abuses. I have set up a review team in the secret room of this office, specializing in reviewing all accounts of the company to ensure that there are no omissions. In addition to the inspectors, I have added several investigators who are dispatched at any time to various branch offices and ships and warehouses in foreign ports to conduct detailed investigations of various situations for review. As for coal and hardware and other materials, I plan to take open and direct measures. Coal will be ordered directly from major coal mines, and hardware will also be purchased wholesale from overseas, which should be more cost-effective and avoid various abuses. However, because the financial resources are not yet abundant, I have to temporarily purchase from local companies in small quantities at any time. Since the rectification, the income from passenger and cargo freight in April has been slightly stronger than before. Unfortunately, May and June are slack months, and the central government has requisitioned ships for military transport. The ships on the river and sea are not evenly distributed and cannot actively operate. (3) Personnel. Although the company is now under the supervision of the government, it is a business and not an official position. It must be purely commercialized and managed by scientific methods. Therefore, the use of personnel must be based on talent, and it is important to pay attention to personality and old morality first. If one place does not have the right person, there will be abuses in that place. Therefore, it is better to keep the old staff than to change to new staff, because business is definitely not something that outsiders can handle. Although the heads of various departments and important staff members of the company are not all-rounders, they all have considerable knowledge and solid personality. As for the senior crew members, they will be carefully reviewed in the future to avoid repeating the mistakes of the New China ship. However, there is a great lack of shipping professionals. Not only is it difficult to find management talents, but it is also difficult to use the staff of the engine and driving departments appropriately. Among the engine crew, there are still many who have been promoted from copper craftsmen, which is evident in the difficulty. In the past, we mostly borrowed talents from foreign countries, which caused the sovereignty to fall into the hands of others. If we change to Chinese staff, we are often afraid of making mistakes due to insufficient experience. Now, the shipping department has been ordered to recruit these trainees in stages and send them to various ships for on-the-job training for promotion. It is best to select talents based on qualified examinations, and those who are recommended through connections often cannot avoid the sigh of being a mediocre player in an ensemble. (4) Ships and Warehouses. The dilapidated condition of the company's ships has been mentioned before. If the economy is slightly better, it is necessary to add twenty or thirty new ships in order to turn around freely. Now, we can only consider the situation and repair them separately for temporary use. However, when bidding for tenders, various factories deliberately charged high repair costs, leaving almost nothing to come out. The China Merchants Machinery Bureau in Pudong has been shut down for several months and has not yet resumed work. It has always been convenient to undertake various projects for the company. Therefore, I have allocated funds to order it to resume work and entrusted the New Feng, New Ming, and Tu Nan ships to the factory for repair, one to save repair costs and one to restore the factory's business. There are not many funds, which is a double benefit. Other ships are still planned to be gradually priced to make them complete. The various wharves and docks are also being planned for repair. The Zhonghua North Three Warehouses have always been used to berth foreign ships. Since Zhao, the former general manager, changed to the manager of the Fourth Warehouse, the credit has plummeted, so that foreign merchants are unwilling to insure and banks are unwilling to accept drafts. The Chinese warehouses have been idle for two years and no one has paid attention to them. The business has plummeted. This is not easy to restore without a large amount of capital. Now, the South Warehouse, namely Jinliyuan Wharf, is being used as a model warehouse for preliminary reorganization, banning theft and leakage to benefit merchants. However, the foundation of the wharf is still mixed with the land of Jardine Matheson and Sandetang. Although a lease agreement has been signed, in recent years, disputes have often arisen due to overdue land rent. Fortunately, the address of Sandetang has been purchased by the company and there is no problem. The land of Jardine Matheson, whether leased or purchased, is also under negotiation. The French Concession has recently had negotiations on the garbage wharf problem, which has encroached on property rights. I am also negotiating strongly, and it has not been resolved yet. I will report on the results later. (5) Assets. The total assets of the company are estimated to be worth about 50 million taels according to the current market price. The foundation cannot be said to be weak. It is only that we have not thought about fundamentally generating profits. Although we have huge assets, we are poor day and night, just like the saying "holding a golden bowl and begging for food." Now, I plan to thoroughly liquidate all assets in various ports, regardless of whether they are related to the shipping industry, and plan to run profitable businesses so that there is no abandonment. The annual rental income will gradually increase, and the assets will also increase accordingly. Even if it is absolutely necessary to sell some assets unrelated to the shipping industry in the future, the prices will be better than they are now.

Fundamental Reorganization Plan. In short, to make the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company revive, we must design from the root, without any doubt. The above-mentioned points are only palliative measures. We are reorganizing the current situation, and many of them are things that have been delayed in the past or have been done but not completed. At this time, we have to make up for them one by one. For example, the case of the encroachment on the Lotus Pond property of Zhenjiang, the case of the Tonghua ship hitting and sinking the Xinji Company sailing boat for compensation, and the case of the company's arrears in the price of hardware after the collapse of the Yuanchang Kun Company are all lawsuits that have been going on for years and have been in dispute for months. Some are still in contention, and some have already lost the lawsuit. Now, they are all being cleared up one by one, and the company is not suffering any losses. There are many other kinds of entanglements. I am planning to clear them up one by one. Even the most important budget of the company has not been established. Various important regulations are still lacking. Although they are ordinary things that should be done within the scope of my duties, because they have not been done in the past, it is like creating something out of nothing. It will not be completed without a considerable amount of time. It is like a person who is seriously ill and has been harmed by medicine, or has been delayed for a long time and has suffered from external feelings. We must first slowly relieve the wrong medicine, remove the miscellaneous feelings, and mix it with ginseng porridge to revive it. Then, we can discuss the way to treat the root cause, and we can find a way. Otherwise, a mess of silk threads will be more difficult to clean up. I will respectfully present to you the predetermined direction of progress in the future and formulate a fundamental plan for reorganizing the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. (1) Increase new capital. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company now wants to restore vitality and activate blood vessels. Without urgently adding capital, it will not be effective. This matter is of great importance. A cup of water is difficult to quench thirst. We must increase new capital of 30 to 50 million to be effective. How easy is it to talk about such a large amount of money? We look to the government and discuss with the shareholders, but we cannot do anything about it. It is almost hopeless in the country. We have no choice but to look to overseas Chinese compatriots, hoping that they have this power. I have seen that in recent years, the patriotic enthusiasm of overseas Chinese has been soaring. They often regret that they cannot see the merchant ships of their motherland fluttering the national emblem and galloping in the ocean in distant foreign lands. After the Shanghai Anti-Japanese War, their donations and funds exceeded tens of millions. If we can use this patriotic psychology to add overseas Chinese capital and cooperate with the old shareholders, it is a great opportunity. Moreover, there are many Cantonese shareholders in the company who have close relationships with overseas Chinese merchants, which is easy to approach. I, Guojie, have sent people to discuss this plan with overseas Chinese in the South Seas Islands, and they have all expressed their approval. However, because the nature of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has not been determined and it is in a precarious situation, they have shown some doubts. If someone is responsible, it is not difficult to have a successful hope. (2) Absorb foreign capital. It has long been determined by the government to absorb foreign capital and develop all domestic production industries. Foreign debt is not impossible to borrow, but it must be used for profit. The company's assets are all over the provinces, but they are mostly abandoned because there is no money to cultivate them. If we can use other people's capital to develop for us, the benefits of building what we get are immeasurable. In August 1928, when the Ministry of Transportation convened a national transportation conference, I, Guojie, contributed this idea, planning to use foreign capital to upgrade and build the Zhonghua North Three Wharves as a foundation for promoting foreign shipping. It has already been taken into account. Now, I plan to use the collection of overseas Chinese capital as the body and the borrowing of foreign capital as the use. Recently, there have been several informal contacts with major merchants from various countries to borrow money. It can be realized only if the company's fundamental plan is determined. (3) Expand domestic shipping. Based on the above two plans, if the finances are indeed in order, then we should add dozens of new ships with larger tonnage, open up shipping routes to various ports in the inland rivers and outer seas, build wharves and warehouses everywhere so that they are all brand new, and build docks and add machine factories to expand domestic shipping as much as possible to prepare for recovering shipping rights. (4) Open up overseas shipping. Now, if our country's merchant ships suddenly think of crossing the Pacific and Atlantic Oceans and competing with European and American countries, not only do we not have this ambition, but it is also a pipe dream. At this time, we cannot plan broadly, but the South Seas area, Saigon, Bangkok, Singapore, Binalanong, Philippines, Java, Batavia, Manila, and other ports, are full of overseas Chinese, and the business is huge. The rice, sugar, coal, tin paper, fur, wood, and groceries produced are the main exports. It is not impossible to open up shipping routes to and from these ports. Therefore, when domestic shipping has gradually expanded, we should expand to various ports in the South Seas. We plan to set two routes first, one from Shanghai through Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, Haiphong, Saigon, Bangkok, Singapore, and Binalanong to the west, and the other from Shanghai through Xiamen, Shantou, Singapore, and Batavia to the south. Each route is scheduled to have two ships of 8,000 tons each, sailing on schedule, one to comfort the long-standing desire of overseas Chinese merchants, and one to seek the development of overseas trade, which is a step that should be taken in the plan. (5) Run sea and land intermodal transport. For sea transport, in addition to the major ports in the South Seas, through Annam, Myanmar, and Siam, in the future, there should be direct shipping routes from this company. As for the Philippines, Sumatra, Borneo, Java, Manila, and other places, there are overseas Chinese organizations that operate shipping companies, and we should contact them to run intermodal transport to expand business. The North Sea shipping route should be promoted even more. We should contact the Russian commercial fleet company in Vladivostok to run intermodal transport to collect the profits of the Siberian Railway and the Chinese Eastern Railway. As for land transport, we should stipulate intermodal transport methods with major railways in the country, properly formulate regulations, and abide by them to show the government's intention to maintain subsidies. (6) Cultivate shipping professionals. The lack of shipping talents is the biggest shame of our country and the reason for the company's decline. Since the closure of the Wusong Merchant Marine School in the first year of the Republic, there has been no place to produce such talents. The scale of the China Merchants Public School is small, and the funding is insufficient. The Huajia Training Ship, which was taken over and continued, was seized by warlords midway, and all the work was wasted. When Zhao, the former general manager, changed to set up a shipping specialty, it was only because of its humble and simple facilities, easy courses, and short-term students, which was not a plan to truly cultivate talents. I, Guojie, believe that in the company's fundamental plan, talents are the most fundamental of the fundamentals. We should urgently establish a most magnificent merchant marine school, with departments of management, navigation, and engine, with at least enough capacity for 1,000 students, and attach several training ships to sail to various ports on the river and sea in stages and train in each class. We must make small achievements within five years, and within ten years, all the talents of the company will be students of this project. We must also follow the precedents of the customs and postal services to formulate treatment and incentive rules to protect the law, make the best use of their talents, use their learning appropriately, and there will be no omissions. To sum up the above six items, if we can follow the Russian Five-Year Plan or the Turkish Three-Year Plan, focus on responsibility, and set a deadline, the company's future will have the hope of rejuvenation. Apart from the nature and status of the company, which will be presented separately, I deeply hope that this fundamental reorganization plan can be deployed by me, Guojie, gradually implemented, guided by your supervision, and that the road will be far away, so that it will not be abandoned halfway, and that the work of building a mountain will not be lost to a basket of soil. I dare not underestimate my ignorance and rudeness. I will carefully present the true state of illness of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the general reorganization situation since taking office, and the proposed fundamental plan to your review, and respectfully request that it be presented to the Minister and instructed to obey. Respectfully presented to Chen, Vice Minister of Transportation and Supervisor of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Li Guojie, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company.

[Producing Film on Cholera] 105

At this time when cholera is rampant, the general public is unaware of the source of the disease and methods of prevention. Once infected, they do not know to choose the correct doctor for treatment, resorting to scraping or taking medicines that do not match the symptoms, leading to worsening conditions and counterproductive results, which are common occurrences. Mr. Du Yuesheng, in order to make the general public understand and promote awareness, specially collaborated with the Red Cross Cholera Hospital on North Xizang Road and the Star Film Company to film how cholera spreads, how scraping leads to worsening conditions, and how treatment can lead to recovery. They have been filming day and night at the hospital for several days, capturing all aspects of dietary hygiene, the suffering of infection, the dangers of scraping, and the hospital's facilities, such as ambulances, injections, treatments, emergency shots, and saline drips. Filming has been completed, and it is said that it will be screened soon to broaden publicity.

Treating a Child's Diarrhea with Opium Pods:

Resulting in the Death of the Child

Dai Hegui's five-year-old daughter, Cai Bao, who lived at No. 63 Huanghe Road in the French Concession, recently suffered from severe diarrhea. Her mother, Ms. Song, believing that opium could treat diarrhea, gave the child an opium pod to swallow the day before yesterday. However, the child was young and weak, and the excessive dose caused poisoning, leading to a critical condition. She was immediately sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, but to no avail. She died in the hospital at 5:15 yesterday morning. The hospital notified the police, who transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Mortuary for examination. Subsequently, the deceased's parents petitioned the police to waive the examination and allow them to handle the matter themselves. The police chief approved their request, and they proceeded to coffin and bury the body in the afternoon.

Minutes of the 114th Meeting of the Lawyers Association's Executive and Supervisory Committee

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its 114th joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committee members at 5 PM the day before yesterday at its office on Route Belles-sur-Mer (Lafayette Road) in the French Concession. Committee members Shen Junru, Yan Yinwu, Tang Hao, Shi Liang, Chen Tingrui, Zhang Zhengxue, Lu Dingkui, Zhang Zhirang, Yang Zhihao, Jiang Jiemin, Li Shirui, Zhu Fuju, and others attended. Lu Dingkui was elected as chairman, and Dai Jixian served as the recorder. The motions are recorded below:

(1) A letter from the First Special District Court of Shanghai forwarding the resolution of disciplinary action against lawyer Lu Ji, requesting notification. (Resolution) Notify Lawyer Lu immediately.

(2) A letter from the First Special District Court of Shanghai requesting the dispatch of personnel to inspect the opium burning case. (Resolution) Committee member Zhang Zhirang is assigned to inspect.

(3) A letter from the Jiangning Lawyers Association regarding the assault case of lawyer Wu Mai, stating that it has been resolved and unanimous continued assistance will be provided, requesting review. (Resolution) File for record.

(4) Committee member Tan Yigong's letter resigning as an elected executive committee member, requesting the next highest alternate executive committee member be appointed. (Resolution) Reserved.

(5) Member Yao Tingguang's report that lawyer Gu Kenfu was fined 50 yuan for suspicion of defamation and whether his right to appear in court should be suspended. (Resolution) Upon review, suspending the right to appear in court is inconsistent with the articles of association. Respond to member Yao for review.

(6) Member Liu Mingdu's letter requesting the joint effort of other professional organizations to oppose the Public Concession Telephone Bureau's charging lawyers' telephone fees as business telephones. (Resolution) File for record.

(7) Member Wu Chengyu's letter responding to the actual situation of lawyer Qu Zheng's lawsuit of ignoring reconciliation, and member Qu Zheng's letter requesting the return of the original file regarding lawyer Wu Chengyu's ignoring reconciliation, regardless of whether a reply is given. (Resolution) Return the original file and copy member Wu Chengyu's original letter to member Qu Zheng for review.

(9) Member Zhang Zhenwan's letter responding to the actual situation of the Lu Zhenhuan fraud and forgery case. (Resolution) Notify the original reporter for review.

(10) Sheng Fangchen's letter inquiring about the handling of the previous report against lawyer Lan Ren for withholding evidence. (Resolution) Send a letter urging lawyer Lan Ren to reply.

(11) Peng Juzhou's report that the Municipal Public Security Bureau is interfering with the judiciary, requesting measures to stop it. (Resolution) File for record.

(12) Committee member Chen Tingrui proposed sending a letter to the court to pay attention to the following points: (A) Court hearings often do not adhere to the designated time (this point should be directed solely to the Second Special District and District Courts). (B) Emergency measures are often delayed, resulting in a loss of actual effectiveness. (C) Regarding the execution of cases, it is recommended that each court handle cases expeditiously in accordance with the instructions of the Ministry of Judicial Administration. (D) Regarding the delivery of documents, especially the decisions of provisional injunctions and provisional attachments, they should be printed and delivered promptly after they are made. The notification of court dates and summonses for the parties should be issued as early as possible. (Items 2, 3, and 4 should be uniformly suggested to each court). All of the above cases, (Resolution) Passed.

(13) Lawyers Qu Zengze, Xu, Chen Xun, Zhang Shanle, Huang Zong, Sun Penghua, Zhang Guoying, Li Jichuan, Chen Bangliang, and others applied for membership. (Resolution) Passed.

The meeting adjourned after all items were discussed.

Provincial Order Restricting Additional Tax Levies on Land Tax

Recently, additional tax levies on land tax in various regions have often been several times more than the regular tax, increasing the burden on the people year after year. The Shanghai County Government received instructions from the Department of Civil Affairs yesterday to restrict these levies. The original order stated: "For compliance matters, it is hereby ordered that an investigation reveals that the additional tax levies on land tax in various counties are many times, or at least double, the regular tax revenue, increasing the burden on the people year after year. Strict restrictions are necessary to demonstrate prudence and compassion. It is hereby stipulated that from the 21st year of the Republic onwards, any increase in the burden on the people must first have the proposed project submitted to the responsible department for approval, and then the transferred funds must be submitted to the responsible department for review. If there are no violations, it should then be submitted to the provincial government for discussion to demonstrate restriction. In addition to separate distribution, it is hereby ordered that the county magistrate comply and instruct subordinates to comply without fail. Sincerely, this order, etc., has been received. In addition to separate distribution, it is hereby ordered that the county magistrate comply and instruct subordinates to comply without fail."

Case of Interference with Family and Enticement

Lin Ahua, a native of Ningbo, recently filed a complaint with the Second Special District Court, accusing Yue Agui, who runs the Xinyi Clothing Store at No. Xin Xin Li on Kim Shenfu Road, of interfering with his family and enticement, among other charges. The court held a hearing yesterday afternoon. The plaintiff stated that he married Yue Xiaoxiang, a 19-year-old cousin of Yue Agui, in the 19th year of the Republic. Later, she was bewitched by the defendant, using the excuse of returning to Ningbo and has been gone for a long time. She came to Shanghai in March of last year and returned to Ningbo in October, encouraged by the defendant. In November, she returned to Shanghai and suddenly disappeared. Later, he learned that she had remarried under the direction of the defendant, thus interfering with his family. He pleaded for punishment, etc. The defendant also entrusted the lawyer Quan Ren to state the defense, claiming that Yue Xiaoxiang is Yue Agui's younger sister, not a cousin. Last October, their mother saw that their relationship was deteriorating and temporarily took her home to ease family disputes, not at the defendant's suggestion. As for encouraging her to return to Ningbo, there was no such thing. Moreover, Xiaoxiang has not remarried. To establish a charge of enticement, there must be enticement. Xiaoxiang came home because of the plaintiff's abuse, and she was advised many times. Xiaoxiang said that if she were to return to the Lin family, she would rather die here. The defendant, out of affection for his sister, temporarily kept and cared for her. How can this be called enticement? Moreover, the word "enticement" refers to inducing and exploiting a person's mistakes while having the power to control them. Now that the defendant has neither induced nor exploited a person's mistakes, how can this be called enticement? Furthermore, Article 13, Paragraph 3 of the General Principles of the Civil Code stipulates that even a minor who is married has the capacity to act and cannot be considered to have committed this crime. Therefore, Judicial Yuan Interpretation No. 414 states that once a minor is married, they have the capacity to act and there is no issue of separation from their parental rights. Those who entice underage men and women do not constitute a crime under Article 257 of the Criminal Code, etc. Since further evidence is needed, the hearing was adjourned.

Young Woman Conning for Money

Zhang Guangyu, an employee of the Municipal Bureau of Education, who lives at No. 34 Borton Village on Route du Père Robert in the French Concession, was visited at 10:30 yesterday morning by a young woman, about 27 or 28 years old, with a dark complexion, wearing high-heeled leather shoes, and a new-style white rayon cheongsam, carrying a colorful parasol. She first claimed to be visiting and said that she also worked in the Second Section of the Bureau of Education, and was a colleague of Mr. Zhang. Today, she had taken a day off because her child was sick and was accompanying the child for treatment. She needed to borrow ten yuan because she did not have enough money for medical expenses, promising to return it tomorrow. Mr. Zhang's family knew that there were female employees in the Bureau and, since her story sounded credible, they believed her and paid the amount. When Mr. Zhang returned home from work, his family told him the story, and Mr. Zhang knew that there was no such woman in the Bureau, so he realized he had been cheated. He hopes that people from all walks of life will pay attention and, if similar incidents occur again, detain the woman.

Smuggling and Selling Poisonous Gas Guns Sentenced to Three Years Each

The three Japanese men, Kono, Taniguchi, and Nakama, smuggled poisonous gas guns to Shanghai and colluded with Ningbo native Xu Zailin and Shaoxing native Tian Chunian to sell them secretly. Song Bingzheng, an inspector from the Narcotics Suppression Department of the Public Works Department, along with detectives Ding Yugao and Chen Yaoting, learned of this and apprehended the five Chinese and Japanese smugglers in Room 511 of the Huizhong Hotel on Hankou Road, confiscating nine poisonous gas guns and over two hundred bottles of poisonous liquid. They were sent separately to the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai and the First Special District Court for detention and trial. This has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the three Japanese men have been interrogated by the Japanese Consulate and confirmed to have engaged in smuggling. However, they were only detained for one week before being deported back to their country with a light sentence. The poisonous guns and poisonous liquid were returned to the Japanese men to take back to Japan. Yesterday morning, the police, noting that the case of the Japanese defendants had been concluded, escorted the two Chinese defendants, Xu and Tian, to the First Special District Court. Judge Qian conducted the trial. The police lawyer, Lv Rubao, stated that the three Japanese men had been interrogated by the consulate and that the defendants had jointly sold poisonous gas guns, which are prohibited internationally. The evidence was solid, and severe punishment should be imposed. Judge Qian then questioned the two defendants, Xu and Tian, who both confessed without dispute. The court immediately sentenced them each to three years in prison. The number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed will be deducted from the prison term at a rate of two days for one day. The police lawyer stated that the number of days of detention of each defendant in the capital should also be deducted. The court approved.

Private Primary Schools in the Concession Ordered to Improve

The Municipal Bureau of Education, noting that private primary schools in the concession are numerous, has found that while many have registered in accordance with regulations, many others have not completed the registration process. These unregistered primary schools have corrupt practices and numerous shortcomings. If they are not regulated and rectified, it will not only fail to benefit the children seeking education but also disrupt the education system. Therefore, the Bureau has specially selected its employees to conduct inspections by district, eliminating the bad and preserving the good to facilitate improvement. It has been found that the Chengde Primary School run by Zhou Gongxiang at No. 241 South Chengdu Road, the Demao Primary School run by Wang Xungao of Suzhou opposite the Yangshupu Road Foreign Affairs Bureau, the Siming Huaide Primary School run by Zhang Shiqing of Ningbo at No. 238 Changqing Lane on Tongzhou Road, the Jiaotong Primary School run by Xu Jin at No. 38 Wenzhou Road, and the Jiying Primary School run by Zhang Mingyi at No. 395 Qipu Road all have issues such as unclean school buildings, poor teaching methods, or a lack of funding. Some even use the school to collect money under false pretenses. The Bureau Director has sent a written request to the First Special District Court to strictly ban these schools and requested that the ban measures be sent back for review. The court recently issued summonses, delivered by the political department of the General Police Department, sending Detective Pan Lianbi to notify each school principal to appear in court for questioning. However, Xu Jin of Jiaotong has already closed the school and his whereabouts are unknown. The school site has now been changed to Jinling Primary School by Qian Zhifan. Zhang Mingyi of Jiying has also closed the school and Zhang has gone to Wuhan. Therefore, only Zhang Shiqing of Siming and Zhou Gongxiang of Chengde appeared in court yesterday morning. Wang Xungao of Demao sent a lawyer as a representative. Judges Wu Tingqi and Fu Lin opened court in the Second and Fourth Tribunals, respectively, for the trial. Zhang Shiqing admitted that he was willing to improve in the future and comply with all regulations. Zhou Gongxiang requested a two-week deadline to start rectification to comply with the regulations. Wang's lawyer also stated the same. The judges ordered the summoned parties to leave and submit a detailed report on the improvement situation for the Municipal Bureau of Education to review.

Russian Watchman Commits Suicide Due to World-Weariness

The Russian watchman, Kraiteikov, age 31, of the Meiqing Leather Company at No. 400 Qiwupu Road in East Shanghai, previously served as a soldier under Zhang Zongchang. Last year, he was introduced by his friend, Kemmen, to work as a watchman at the company. The Russian man suddenly felt weary of the world because he thought his income was too meager. At around 5:00 AM, he shot himself in the chest with his own pistol in his bedroom, falling to the ground in extreme pain with blood gushing out. Li Haizhu, a Chinese clerk, heard the sound and rushed over, horrified at the sight. He immediately reported to the police, who dispatched Western detective and Chinese detective Ma Wenda to investigate. They found a suicide note in the bedroom, which read, "I never wanted to work here, but I have two beloved dogs, please take care of them." He was then transported to Gongji Hospital, but had already died. The body was taken to the forensic examination center on Fielan Road. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei of the First Special District Court came to the center for examination. According to the testimony of witness Li Haizhu, at 5:30 that morning, he was washing his face when he suddenly heard a gunshot from the deceased's bedroom. He rushed to see what had happened and saw the deceased lying on the ground with a gunshot wound. He touched him and felt a faint breath, so he reported to the police. The Western and Chinese detectives reported the details of the investigation and presented the suicide note. The American manager of the Meiqing Company, Mr. Meiersen, stated that the deceased was indeed a watchman for the company and requested to claim the body for burial. Mr. Guo approved, ruling that the deceased Russian, Kraiteikov, had indeed committed suicide with a pistol before his death, and the body was handed over to Mr. Meiersen for burial after he signed a guarantee.

Retrial and Sentencing in the Assassination of Ling Runxiang Case

The case of Ling Runxiang, a Guangdong native and director of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, being assassinated by gunfire at the entrance of Dexing Lane on North Jiangxi Road at 6:00 PM on July 28, 1920. The five Guangdong natives, Ou Zhaocheng (i.e. Ou Zhaocheng), Liu Xizhuang, Luo Baoliang, Ou Chang, and Ou Chuntong were apprehended by Feng Shuofu, a Chinese detective in the Hongkou Police Department, on August 4 of the same year at the Guangwutai Theater in the Chinese territory. They were then handed over to the Garrison Headquarters, sentenced as military prisoners, and sent to the capital for execution. Later, family members hired lawyers to request the Ministry of Military Affairs to send the case to the Jiangning District Court to overturn the original verdict for a retrial. Since the location of the Ling case and the arrest of the criminals, Lu Ju, etc., were all in the Shanghai concession, the court sent the five men to the Hongkou Police Department on June 8 of this year to be handed over to the First Special District Court. After repeated trials, it was found that the murderer was Hu Ying, who was still at large. The court then announced the end of the defense and sentencing process. Yesterday morning, Judge Fu Lin opened court and announced that defendant Ou Zhaocheng was found guilty of premeditated murder and sentenced to twelve years in prison, Liu Xizhuang, Ou Chang, and Ou Chuntong were found guilty of conspiracy to murder and sentenced to five years in prison each, and Luo Baoliang was sentenced to three years in prison. The number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed will be deducted from the prison term at a rate of two days for one day. The police lawyer stated that the number of days of detention of each defendant in the capital should also be deducted. The court approved.

The 20th District Branch of the Citizens Association Opposes Telephone Price Increase

The 20th District Branch of the Citizens Association, in response to the telephone price increase in the concession, yesterday specially notified its members to fill out volunteer forms to gather public opinion and negotiate accordingly. It also sent a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers Association in the Concession, forwarding it to the Chinese Directors of the Public Works Department for negotiation. The letter stated: "To the esteemed sirs, since the Japanese invasion of Zhabei on January 28, the businesses in our northeastern district have been completely destroyed. Even the shops in the central district, although not directly ravaged by the Japanese, have suffered significant indirect effects due to the stagnation of the market for more than two months. Now, as we are preparing to restore the market and strive for commercial recovery, the realization of the telephone price increase, which is most important to commerce, is causing deep concern. We believe that the telephone is a public utility and has a monopolistic nature. It should strive for the benefit of the public. How can it take advantage of its monopolistic position to seek private gain and implement a price increase, disregarding the interests of the public? At a time when commerce is depressed after the war, increasing the price of telephones is a violation of the original purpose of public utilities. The company claims to be upgrading to automatic machines and intends to pass the cost on to users, but this reason is insufficient. Upgrading to automatic machines is a facility for the company to develop its business. The profits earned over the years should be used for this purpose. Moreover, in the future, as shops find it more convenient to communicate, they will inevitably install telephones, and the revenue will be considerable. In short, such price increases are entirely one-sided. The company is only seeking profit and disregarding the burden on users. The Public Works Department should not disregard the ability of taxpayers to pay, ignore legal principles and human feelings, and rashly approve the increase. We are sending this special letter to your association, requesting that you forward it to the Public Works Department for reconsideration and request the Chinese Directors present to argue strongly for the cancellation of the price increase in order to alleviate commercial difficulties and benefit the market."

Painter and Calligrapher Ma Mengrong Returns to Shanghai

Ma Mengrong of Yongjia and his younger brother, Gongyu, are both famous at home and abroad for their calligraphy, painting, and epigraphy. Mengrong inherited his family's scholarship and created his own style in painting flowers, birds, grass, insects, fish, and crabs, which is unique and transcendent. His landscapes and figures have high artistic merit, and his inscriptions and calligraphy are also highly praised. Society has long recognized his talent, and there is no need to elaborate further. This spring, he returned to his hometown to avoid the war and lived in seclusion, engaging in writing. However, requests for his paintings and calligraphy from other places continued unabated, even from Guizhou, Guangxi, and overseas, with people bringing money to seek his works. Now, at the request of connoisseurs and his disciples, and at the invitation of the China Arts and Crafts Society, he returned to Shanghai yesterday and is staying at No. 55 Mingde Lane, Foch Road. Mr. Ma has many years of teaching experience and is well-experienced. Those who wish to study painting can contact him at his residence. He will resume accepting commissions tomorrow. His collection points are at various paper fan stores and at his residence.

Letter to the Editor

To the Editor:

I read the "Harbor Quarantine Dispute" in your newspaper's local news section, which does not match the facts. According to nautical practice and harbor quarantine regulations, all matters related to the voyage and port quarantine are the responsibility of the shipowner. The reason why the quarantine medical officer ordered the police to detain the Xinfeng was because the chief mate of the ship, Jiang Changqing, was unfamiliar with nautical regulations and disobeyed the shipowner's orders, abusing his authority. Since the January 28 Incident in Shanghai and the subsequent discovery of cholera outbreaks in various ports, all imported ships have been quarantined in the harbor. The number of ships inspected daily often ranges from a dozen to more than twenty. The procedures and methods for quarantine have already been announced in Announcement No. 24 by this office and communicated to Chinese and foreign shipping companies for compliance. The report stated that the Xinfeng arrived at the Jinliyuan Wharf at 8:40 AM yesterday (July 25), but the medical officer of this office did arrive on board at 8:45 AM, without any dereliction of duty. The shipowner's signed document can be used as verification. As they were preparing to implement the quarantine work, the chief mate Jiang came out and rebuked the medical officer of this office for being troublesome and pulled down the quarantine yellow flag. In order to maintain the quarantine regulations and maintain order, the medical officer had to summon the police for protection and reported to the office. Later, Director Wang of the Shipping Department of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company came to mediate. Director Wu, considering that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is a state-run shipping company and that the ignorant and violating chief mate Jiang is also a fellow compatriot, did not impose strict punishment in order to safeguard the national image and support the younger generation of the shipping industry. He only ordered the chief mate Jiang Changqing to personally apologize to the office to settle the matter. This is the true situation of the dispute from beginning to end. Since this office took over the harbor quarantine, shipping companies from all countries have praised and complied. However, some domestic shipping companies lack this level of awareness and often cause disputes, which is regrettable. Therefore, this office often provides various conveniences to the domestic shipping industry, hoping for cooperation to avoid internal conflicts and ridicule, so as to enhance our international standing. Thinking that your newspaper's editorial standards are high, perhaps the reporting was not detailed enough, leading to errors in transmission. This letter is sent to you in the hope that you will make corrections. Sincerely, Harbor Quarantine Administration, July 26, 21st year of the Republic.

Letter to the Editor

Basic Principles of Railway Responsibility for Transportation Regulations (Continued)

Zheng Baozhao

(G) Special services that the carrier is not required to provide by law. The shipper only has the right to require the public carrier to accept and transport the goods in the usual and customary manner, and cannot force the carrier to provide special services or transport them in a manner different from that used to treat the general public. If any carrier provides any special privilege business due to special contact, it is considered not to be within the scope of its responsibility, to fulfill the obligation of a public carrier, and will not be responsible for the liability of the insurer.

(H) Types of public carriers. The method used by the carrier for transportation is not a condition for determining whether it is a public carrier. The question of whether it is a public carrier depends on whether the carrier is willing to lease freight and transport the goods of the public. The general opinion is that express companies are not public carriers, because express companies do not directly transport the goods themselves, but indirectly transport them through railways, ships, or other carriers. The company itself has no way to intervene, cannot send employees or agents to manage the goods that have arrived, and cannot exercise any supervision over such employees or agents. However, in court, express companies are considered to be public carriers, because the contract for public carriers does not require that the transportation must be completed entirely under the direct guidance and management of the carrier itself. Any public carrier may choose to transport the goods themselves or entrust an agent to transport them under their supervision and management. If the situation exceeds this, a separate contract must be drawn up to specify the details. Therefore, it is appropriate for the court to recognize express companies as public carriers, because although the company itself does not transport the goods, it entrusts railways, ships, or other carriers to transport them under its supervision, which is the same as transporting them themselves. As for the nature of delivery companies, which is quite similar to that of express companies, they are also regarded as public carriers

Fate had it that the couple encountered each other. She had also run to Old Woman Wang's place. Old Woman Wang only knew Mr. Xie and did not recognize Mrs. Xie. Moreover, she had always used an alias when visiting, for fear of Old Woman Wang blabbing it out. So, she changed her name. Today, she didn't know that her husband was also here, so she had come boldly. Who knew that in the middle of their performance, she would suddenly be caught by her husband. Fortunately, she immediately saw that her husband was also coming out of a room with another woman standing beside him, so she knew that her husband was also doing the same kind of thing. Instantly, she became a hundred times bolder and immediately voiced the above rational protest. "Ugh...ugh..." He was rendered speechless by his wife's words. Japanese Residents Refuse Household Registration Investigation 106

City Government Transfers Case to Japanese Consulate for Negotiation

After the withdrawal of Japanese troops from Zhabei in this city, the Municipal Public Security Bureau immediately began investigating

Page 16

household registrations. This has now been completed. However, in the area of the Mixed Court District, many Japanese residents refused to accept the household registration investigation when the Municipal Public Security Bureau went to investigate. As a result, the foreign household population statistics are still pending. The Municipal Public Security Bureau, considering this matter of great importance, specifically petitioned the City Government to negotiate with the Japanese Consul. The City Government, after receiving the petition, yesterday transferred a letter to Japanese Consul Murai for negotiation. The original letter is recorded below: Respectfully, the case is based on the report from the Municipal Public Security Bureau stating, according to the report from He Yiming, the district chief of the Fifth District, that the household registration inspector Jia Wenbin reported that about a hundred Japanese households in Lane 164 and Lane 236 of Baole'an Road, Yuqingli, and Yong'anli of North Sichuan Road in his jurisdiction jointly refused to fill out the forms. The proper procedure was requested. In addition to instructing the inspector to persuade them tactfully and continue the investigation, it is proper to report the situation and request examination and compliance. Previously, according to the report from the director of the Household Registration Section of this Bureau, a letter has been sent to the takeover committee for negotiation. Now, according to the aforementioned report, in addition to the instruction, it is proper to report the situation and request examination and approval to facilitate the case negotiation, which is in the public interest. Therefore, this letter is sent to request your review and instruct them to fill out the forms in accordance with the case for protection. We look forward to your reply.

Public Concession June Sanitary Overview 107

The Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department's June report states that the death rate for foreigners this month was 8.43 per thousand, and the death rate for Chinese was 9.98 per thousand. This is the lowest figure in twenty-five years. The number of deaths from infectious diseases in June compared to May is as follows: Cholera, in May, 25 cases, 1 death, percentage was 4; in June, 342 cases, 31 deaths, percentage was 9. Other infectious diseases, in May, 337 cases, 152 deaths, percentage was 45; in June, 348 cases, 149 deaths, percentage was 43. Since June 6, cholera has reached epidemic proportions, but the number of deaths is not high, perhaps because the nature of this cholera is milder or because of stronger resistance. The cause of cholera is quite complex and not easily understood without thorough research. Generally speaking, it can be divided into two types: short-term and chronic. "Short-term" is also a comparative term. As for the plague in Shanghai, it has developed more slowly this year compared to other locations. Regarding prevention work, it was inconvenient to administer injections in June due to heavy rainfall, but still 59,332 people were injected, totaling 87,270 people. Those injected by other organizations are not included in this number. In June, 600 wells were disinfected by the Health Department, but this measure also has drawbacks. If the amount of medicine used is insufficient, it can easily make drinkers careless, and because of the odor, it may even lead people to drink other water. However, drinking water is not the only source of cholera, so the method of prevention cannot be achieved overnight. Regarding this matter, cracking down on street vendors is an important issue. The crackdown on street vendors must be carried out in conjunction with the establishment of markets. We have been actively proceeding to the best of our ability. Two more will be built this year. Also, poor boat dwellers are a major problem that the Public Concession cannot solve alone. Dredging rivers, supplying clean water, and public education are all problems. Due to incomplete reporting, effective isolation cannot be carried out at the point of the outbreak. In addition, of other infectious diseases, smallpox has greatly decreased. There were 24 reported cases of scarlet fever. 65 Chinese people died of tuberculosis. There is nothing else noteworthy. The pathology laboratory was quite busy this month. There were 62 cases of plague treatment, four of whom came from other ports. The tuberculosis hospital and the venereal disease hospital were both busy. Regarding food, 105 samples of milk and cream were tested, and 87 were qualified. Four herds of cattle were inspected, and eight herds were tested for tuberculosis. The number of slaughters at the bureau-established slaughterhouse increased this month. 23 cattle and 13 pigs were discarded. Business at the vegetable markets was as usual, but due to a shortage of meat, butchers were noticeably diminished. Bakeries, ice cream shops, and ice factories were given special attention. 134 types of food were analyzed and tested for mold. A total of 180 cases were prosecuted for violating licensing regulations.

Cholera Outbreak in the Southwestern Suburbs of This City 108

In the southwestern suburbs of this city, in the towns along the Caoxi River, Hongqiao, and Shanghai-Minhang Road, the weather has been extremely hot in recent days. Farmers working in the fields under the scorching sun have developed a plague. Patients experience simultaneous vomiting and diarrhea, abdominal pain like being twisted, and the infection spreads extremely quickly. Some die within moments without being treated. In the past two days, dozens of men and women have died from cholera. Local officials are now administering vaccinations to prevent the spread of the epidemic, and purchasing large quantities of Shada medicine water, distributing it to various villages. It is also known that Caohejing Town will establish a medical clinic on the 30th of this month, and has hired famous doctors from various departments to provide diagnoses separately.

Summer Epidemic Prevention Compilation 109

The Hongkou Public Epidemic Hospital, thanks to the contributions of Gu Shaoqing, Shen Shaoyu, Cai Xinjing, Cai Zhufang, and Han Pihao from the business community, specially requested Dr. Wang Boyuan and others to establish the Public Epidemic Hospital at the entrance of the small vegetable market on Dongyouheng Road in Hongkou, providing day and night diagnoses. All registration fees, medicine fees, and hospitalization fees are waived. Since its opening, more than a hundred workers from factories in the area and poor residents nearby have sought treatment daily. Recently, a patient named Dai Agen, who was suffering from an epidemic and unconscious for about an hour, was treated by Dr. Wang of the hospital and recovered, it is said.

The Fifth District of the County Organizes Injections and Medical Treatment. Xing Zhigang, the district chief of the Fifth District of Shanghai County, in view of the recent hot weather and the prevalence of epidemics, has hired Western doctors to provide free vaccinations at the major intersections of the towns of Tangkou and Tiqiao under his jurisdiction. Furthermore, considering that farmers working in the fields are exposed to the scorching sun and suffer from heatstroke and various seasonal illnesses, and that the poor and sick are unable to seek medical treatment, he has specially invited renowned doctors from various departments, including Hu Youxin, Wang Sicheng, and the female physician Zhang Youfang, to establish a summer medical clinic in Chenhangji, providing free consultations and medication. From July 25th to September 30th, regular diagnoses will be provided. It is said that there are more than two hundred patients every day, which is very crowded, and the local people have benefited greatly.

Recent Situation of Du's Epidemic Hospital 110

Mr. Du Yuesheng, in order to relieve the epidemic and benefit the poor, has taken on the responsibility of establishing five epidemic hospitals this year. The hospital affairs of each hospital are assisted by Dr. Pang Jingzhou. At this time of cholera prevalence, the clinics of each hospital are extremely busy. It is estimated that the Gaoqiao Jiqun Hospital has an average of more than 200 outpatient visits per day, the Lannidu Hospital has more than 100 visits per day, and the Yangjing Hospital also has nearly 100 visits per day. During the epidemic period, the Shanghai North Xizang Road Emergency Epidemic Hospital had more than 300 visits per day, including internal medicine and surgical outpatient visits. Recently, Mr. Du, in view of the severe epidemic in various villages in Pudong, specially established an epidemic hospital in Gaohang Township, which is currently being prepared and will be established soon. The area is densely populated with inadequate sanitation facilities, and many people are suffering from the epidemic. It is expected that there will be more than 100 visits per day. If calculated in this way, the five hospitals will treat 300,000 patients annually, all completely free of charge, benefiting the sick to a great extent.

Recent News from Yangjing Town Epidemic Hospital 111

Yangjing Town in Pudong is densely populated and has many factories. Every summer, epidemic prevention is established to benefit the poor and sick. This year, local gentry, in view of the widespread epidemic after the war, expanded the Yangjing Epidemic Hospital in Baorentang on Baoren Road. They specially hired Dr. Sun Naikang, a top student of the famous Shanghai doctor Pang Jingzhou, as the medical director, and also hired Dr. Feng Guliang, nurses Wu San, Tang Ruirong, pharmacist Huang Zhenxin, and general affairs Huang Shengji to assist. This year, all the equipment in the hospital is more complete than in previous years, including a consultation room, a physiological saline injection room, a dispensing room, a waiting room, a morgue, and multiple wards specifically for admitting epidemic patients day and night, providing diagnoses and medicine free of charge, specializing in internal and external medicine and providing free epidemic prevention injections. It is reported that since the hospital opened on the 5th of this month, it has been less than two weeks, and more than 1,500 patients have been treated, with more than 20 cases of true cholera, all of whom have been cured and discharged. The number of people seeking treatment at the hospital every day is crowded and overwhelming.

Recent News from the Second Red Cross Epidemic Hospital 112

Since the opening of the Second Epidemic Hospital of the Chinese Red Cross Society last month, the number of patients has exceeded 6,000. The original 150 beds have now been increased by 40 due to the increase in inpatients and the lack of space. It is reported that yesterday more than 40 patients needed saline injections. The severity of the epidemic can be imagined. However, it is also because the hospital is located in a suitable location at Zhangjiabang, north of the Racecourse, and the staff are all top choices, so people are happy to seek treatment with the hope of recovery. The telephone number is 31271, and an ambulance is available to pick up patients immediately upon receiving a call, free of charge.
